## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration as a function of position x (and possibly explicit time t), which is the standard setting for 1-DOF oscillator equations derived from Newton’s law with nonlinear restoring forces and/or time-dependent forcing/parametric excitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (Hookean) oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude spring-mass, constant stiffness)
- Biased equilibrium (constant load): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (gravity/offset force shifting equilibrium)
- Quadratic stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 (asymmetric spring restoring due to geometry)
- Cubic stiffness (Duffing, hardening/softening): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (common nonlinear spring model)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (strong nonlinearity / higher-order potential terms)
- Pendulum restoring (exact): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (angular oscillator where x is angle; bounded nonlinearity)
- Saturating/softening restoring via tangent hyperbolic: dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * x) (bounded force at large displacement)
- Piecewise linear stiffness (bilinear spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Max(x - c2, 0) (stiffness change after a gap/stop)
- Non-smooth stiffness using absolute value: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) (odd restoring force with magnitude growing ~|x|^2)
- Dry friction / Coulomb-like restoring component: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(x) (spring plus constant-magnitude opposing force)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (additive periodic drive)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (general periodic excitation basis)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (Mathieu-type parametric resonance form)
- Time-modulated nonlinear stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x**3 (periodically varying Duffing nonlinearity)
- Conservative potential-gradient form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (restoring force as -dV/dx with even polynomial potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about x=0, dv_dt is typically an odd function of x (terms like x, x**3, x*Abs(x), sin(c*x)); even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetry or bias.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: a positive cubic-restoring contribution (more negative dv_dt for large |x|) implies frequency increases with amplitude; a negative cubic term implies softening and potential bistability.
- Bounded restoring force: using sin(c*x) or tanh(c*x) encodes a force that cannot grow unbounded with |x| (e.g., pendulum, geometric saturation).
- Parametric excitation signature: factors like (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) * x indicate stiffness modulation; these often produce resonance tongues and strong time dependence even without additive forcing.
- Additive forcing signature: stand-alone periodic terms in t (e.g., cos(c*t), sin(c*t)) imply an external drive independent of x, producing steady-state oscillations/beat phenomena.
- Non-smooth behavior/impacts: Max(x-c,0), Abs(x), or sign(x) structures suggest contact, backlash, piecewise stiffness, or dry friction leading to sharp changes in acceleration near thresholds.
- Equilibrium shifts: constant terms (c1) or mixed bias terms move the stable equilibrium away from x=0 and can make dv_dt(x=0) nonzero.
- Higher-order polynomial terms: x**5 and beyond indicate strong nonlinearity and can stabilize/unstabilize large-amplitude motion depending on sign and combination with lower-order terms.
